        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer318696364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5267386359055896587"><b>Main characters:</b> <br/>Jane Jameson <br/>Gabriel, Jane’s sire<br/>Zeb, her friend<br/>Richard "Dick" Cheney<br/><br/><b>What I Liked:</b> This is a comedy and, in a way, also a parody of all the vampire books out there. Jane, as you saw in the blurb is an honest to God librarian. She suffers an untimely accident and to keep her from dying Gabriel changes her into a vampire. After this she tries to adapt to the life, and for us, the readers, is hilarious. The writer has a tongue-in-cheek style that is very attractive. I loved “The Gu</span>
  <span id="freeText5267386359055896587" style="display:none"><b>Main characters:</b> <br>Jane Jameson <br>Gabriel, Jane’s sire<br>Zeb, her friend<br>Richard "Dick" Cheney<br><br><b>What I Liked:</b> This is a comedy and, in a way, also a parody of all the vampire books out there. Jane, as you saw in the blurb is an honest to God librarian. She suffers an untimely accident and to keep her from dying Gabriel changes her into a vampire. After this she tries to adapt to the life, and for us, the readers, is hilarious. The writer has a tongue-in-cheek style that is very attractive. I loved “The Guide for the Newly Undead” quotes at the start of each chapter, I think this was what I liked most from the book :D<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/4bwMgqU" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376025i/730744.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Jane’s budding power…</i> <br><br><b>What I didn't like:</b> Too much rambling. There were about at least 10% that were not necessary for the narrative or the characters. The start also was kind of weird and it took me a little to get into the book.<br><br><b>Favorite character:</b> Dick. He’s irreverent and doesn’t take 95% of the things that happen seriously. He’s a great friend to have, always there but also helping to keep your spirits up. His only problem: he sleeps with any female on 2 legs! Besides that I really loved his character, even his man-slut persona is funny :D<br><br><b>My least favorite character:</b> Missy, GOODNESS she was the most annoying character in the history of characters! Even the narrator mad her annoying, that accent almost killed me. <br><br><b>Favorite scene:</b> The telemarketer scene, it was disturbing but very funny! You have to read it to get the humor :D<br><br><b>Favorite quotes:</b> <br>“If you want to hurt me fine. Take my books. Burn down my house. Shave my head while I'm sleeping. But nobody nobody screws with my dog.”<br>….<br>“The love of a good woman can save a man" I remember Gabriel saying. "Or it can drive him to fits of unspeakable madness.” <br>….<br> “The brain may die, but my compulsion for useless trivia lives on.”<br>“Wal-mart started selling "Vampire Home Defense Kits", including holy water, crosses, stakes, mallets, and a book of quick blessings to bar vampires from your door. The fact that these kits were generally useless didn't bother me nearly as much as the idea of holy water being sold at wal-mart.”<br>….<br>“When we were kids, Mama used to ask, “If Zeb wanted to jump off the roof, would you do it, too?” And as it turned out, the answer was yes.”<br>…..<br>“Would you kick her ass already?" Dick said, shoving me back toward Missy. "Come on, Stretch, man up. You do better than this! Get mad."<br>I nodded, rolling a dislocated shoulder back into place with a grunt and staggering back toward my opponent. <br>Behind me, Zeb yelled, "She tried to hurt Fitz!" He turned to Gabriel and Dick. "That'll get her mad."<br>Gabriel rolled his eyes. "She's been framed for murder twice over, shot in the back, her arms were set on fire, and her parents are being held hostage. You think tampered dog water is what's going to make her angry?" <br>"You tried to hurt my dog!" I wheezed as I lurched toward a grinning Missy.”<br><br><b>Would I recommend the book:</b> Yes, it’s a great way to spend time. <br><a href="http://imgur.com/uYyh4ki" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376025i/730745._SY540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Final rating:</b>3.5*<br></span>

<div id="review_1384591257" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1384591257" />
    <a title="Lakshmi C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7678185-lakshmi-c"><img alt="Lakshmi C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540966168p2/7678185.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1384591257?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lakshmi C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lakshmi C" href="/user/show/7678185-lakshmi-c">Lakshmi C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1384591257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10967933129525010171">I have heard lovely things about this book and I started it with Great Expectations...Then I had a strange reading experience .<br/><br/>What I liked : <br/><br/>Jane<br/>Jane was a librarian who got turned in a very embarassing manner. She loved, books, trivia, pizza and her dog Fitz.<br/>Her family was eccentric and interesting, her dad was a supportive professor, her mother was a Savant at being passive aggressive, she had the sister from hell and she was closest to her Aunt Jettie.<br/><br/>Gabriel<br/>He was Jane's sire, patient, prop</span>
  <span id="freeText10967933129525010171" style="display:none">I have heard lovely things about this book and I started it with Great Expectations...Then I had a strange reading experience .<br /><br />What I liked : <br /><br />Jane<br />Jane was a librarian who got turned in a very embarassing manner. She loved, books, trivia, pizza and her dog Fitz.<br />Her family was eccentric and interesting, her dad was a supportive professor, her mother was a Savant at being passive aggressive, she had the sister from hell and she was closest to her Aunt Jettie.<br /><br />Gabriel<br />He was Jane's sire, patient, proper and protective. He had a fabulous past and a coffin full of secrets.<br /><br />Dick Cheney<br />He was Gabriel's arch enemy and damn entertaining, I would love to read more about him. <br /><br />The Guide for the Newly Dead<br />Most of the quotes from this book made me grin :)<br /><br />When you encounter unpleasantness from the human population, try to keep in mind that you will be able to dance on their graves long after they’re dead. It’s a cheering thought.<br /><br />Fine, fine. You know my secret. I have a unicorn collection.”<br /><br />“That’s a very sad secret,” he said as he allowed me to shove his foot from the door.<br /><br />“Strong words coming from someone who was ‘devoured’ by a sea lion.<br /><br /><br />How is your grandma?”<br /><br />“Fine.” Zeb sighed. “Driving my grandpa slowly insane gives her a reason to live.<br /><br /><br />What I didn't like : <br /><br />The story had a mystery but I wasn't even trying to figure out who the Mischief maker was.<br />Troubling, very troubling.<br /><br />The story had some witty one liners, funny sequences but all I managed was a grin.<br /><br />The worst part is I kept comparing it to another vampire series as I read, this got irritating pretty soon.<br /><br />I felt like a spectator as I read this, the mystery didn't pull me in and I felt disconnected from the characters.<br /><br />This could be a case of right book, monstrously wrong time...<br />I will definitely give this series another try after some months</span>
  <a data-text-id="10967933129525010171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6091019144545324764">When I first discovered Goodreads, 4 years ago now, Molly Harper’s <i>The Care and Feeding of Stray Vampires</i> was among the first books I added to my ‘Want To Read’ list and it is currently the oldest book still remaining on there. I discovered that was a spin-off series to this one, and took place later, so I should read this one first. Now I have finally done so (or started to, there’s obviously more books in the series). <br/><br/>It was a bit silly and extremely cliche, let’s be honest, and Jane was a <i>lit</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6091019144545324764" style="display:none">When I first discovered Goodreads, 4 years ago now, Molly Harper’s <i>The Care and Feeding of Stray Vampires</i> was among the first books I added to my ‘Want To Read’ list and it is currently the oldest book still remaining on there. I discovered that was a spin-off series to this one, and took place later, so I should read this one first. Now I have finally done so (or started to, there’s obviously more books in the series). <br /><br />It was a bit silly and extremely cliche, let’s be honest, and Jane was a <i>little</i> eye-roll worthy in parts. But it was also lighthearted fun, quite amusing and entertaining, and goes a way to filling the hole that the <i>Sookie Stackhouse</i> series left. <br /><br />This series would probably make a good pick-me-up for those days you’re feeling a bit down, and I will read the next one. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2654210604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16537598583859599477">Small town librarian, Jane Jameson, loses her job and her life all in one day. Three days later she awakens as a vampire. Besides trying to figure out how she’ll come out to her passive aggressive dysfunctional family, attempting to find a new job, and dating her sexy new sire, Jane struggles to survive; because someone is out to get her. <br/><br/>Although the ending was predictable, the story was quick and fun. Jane’s family really got on my nerves and there were several instances when I wanted her to s</span>
  <span id="freeText16537598583859599477" style="display:none">Small town librarian, Jane Jameson, loses her job and her life all in one day. Three days later she awakens as a vampire. Besides trying to figure out how she’ll come out to her passive aggressive dysfunctional family, attempting to find a new job, and dating her sexy new sire, Jane struggles to survive; because someone is out to get her. <br /><br />Although the ending was predictable, the story was quick and fun. Jane’s family really got on my nerves and there were several instances when I wanted her to show more of a backbone when it came to the women in her life. Since this is the first book in the series, I’m guessing the writer is providing room for character development and lots of growth. At least, that is my hope.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uXVB2cXVTyakZOBmGKkWiqdvc4rapb6Gw+lbgeFaagaV6kwqJ5ENCraTl6xX/WtnhPkw+FjFnM7OD04pq/2QpA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ki4ATmbXD+gHDbCKGK//z0mwez16w46sQeK+EUAGtXm+sQ29hJNNxBX6x0BX+4IiaiY4T/ijrORMBKu5CqFP2w==')})

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2503028.Molly_Harper">About Molly Harper</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2503028.Molly_Harper"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1263196898p3/2503028.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/2503028.Molly_Harper">Molly Harper
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
6,118
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9335893373393276763">My mother remembers an 8-year-old me setting up my “writing office” in our living room by putting her old manual typewriter on the couch next to a toy phone. And I (very slowly) pecked out the story of my third-grade class taking a trip around the world and losing a kid in each city.<br/><br/>I had a dark sense of humor, even then.<br/><br/>In high school, when other girls my age were writing poems about dying unicor</span>
  <span id="freeText9335893373393276763" style="display:none">My mother remembers an 8-year-old me setting up my “writing office” in our living room by putting her old manual typewriter on the couch next to a toy phone. And I (very slowly) pecked out the story of my third-grade class taking a trip around the world and losing a kid in each city.<br /><br />I had a dark sense of humor, even then.<br /><br />In high school, when other girls my age were writing poems about dying unicorns and bleeding roses, I was writing essays about having political arguments with my dad at the dinner table. (Whoever made the other person laugh at their own political party won the argument.) I knew I wanted to write when I grew up, but I also knew there was very little chance I could make a living writing books, so I went for the next best thing – newspaper writing. <br /><br />I majored in print journalism at Western Kentucky University and used my shiny new degree to get a job at my hometown newspaper. I married my high school sweetheart, David, a local police officer. And for six years, I wrote about school board meetings, quilt shows, a man “losing” the fully grown bear he kept as a pet in his basement, and a guy who faked his death by shark attack in Florida and ended up tossing pies at a local pizzeria. <br /><br />I loved my job at the paper. I loved meeting new people every day and never knowing where I would end up. But somehow, the ever-shifting schedules of a police officer and a reporter did not equal "family friendly." One of us needed to take a normal job for the sake of our young daughter. I took a secretarial position at a local church office, which left me with dependably free evenings for the first time in my adult life. David was working the night shift that summer and I was losing.my.mind. We were living in "The Apartment of Lost Souls" while building our new home. This was the place where appliances and small electronics went to die. Every night I would tuck our snoozing child into bed and wait for the washing machine to start smoking or the computer to suddenly flash the "blue screen of death." Then there was the plague of frogs in the bathroom that put our daughter of potty-training for about six months.<br /><br />Normally, when things get tough, I can take solace in reading. But I surveyed my packing box of favorite books with the apathetic air of someone who stands in front of the open refrigerator for 10 minutes and can't find anything. Nothing sounded good. So I just sat down and started writing something I would want to read. <br /><br />Being a huge fan of vampire movies and TV shows, I wondered, what would be the most humiliating way possible to be turned into a vampire- a story that a vampire would be embarrassed to share with their vampire buddies over a nice glass of Type O. Well, first, you'd have to make the protaganist a bit of an accidental loser. She's single, almost 30, and a librarian working in the small Kentucky town where she grew up. This "triple whammy of worry" has made her a permanent fixture on her Mama's prayer list. And despite the fact that's pretty good at her job, she just got canned so her boss could replace her with someone who occasionally starts workplace fires. She drowns her sorrows at the local faux nostalgia-themed sports bar and during the commute home, she's mistaken for a deer and then shot by a drunk hunter. And then she wakes up as a vampire.<br /><br />And thus, Jane Jameson and the wacky denizens of Half-Moon Hollow were born.<br /><br />It took me almost a year to complete and edit a draft of the book, which I planned as the first in a three-book series. I spent three months using agentquery.com to ruthlessly stalk potential literary agents. (There were a lot of lists involved, I don't want to re-live it.) I was gently rejected by at least half of them. I corresponded with some very nice, very patient people, but ultimately signed with the fabulous Stephany Evans of Fine Print Literary Management. Stephany was willing to take to the time to give me advice on how to imp</span>

      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_12098371').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_12098371').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_12098371').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
